ECONOMIC OUTLOOK
ECONOMIC BUSINESS EXPECTATIONS
OUTLOOK The latest business expectations surveys reveal
that manufacturers and service providers expect
business conditions to improve over the next six
months. Nevertheless, partly reflecting seasonal
LEADING INDICATORS patterns, businesses registered less optimism than

(1) Nurturing a Pro-Business SME Credit Bureau
Environment
SME Credit Bureau is Singapore’s first central
Broad-Based Assistance database on credit-related information on SMEs.
It aims to enhance the credit transparency of
SMEs and lessen the challenges they face in
SME First Stop
obtaining financing. It was launched in March
The SME First Stop was set up in 1998 to 2005, together with the Association of Small and
serve as a convenient first point of contact for Medium Enterprises, Singapore Business
SMEs to access information on Government Federation and Infocredit D&B (Singapore) Pte
assistance and regulations governing their Ltd.
business. In 2005, it facilitated some 7,700 cases
SME ACCESS Loan
of enquiries, bringing a total of 61,450 since its
launch.
A new SME financing scheme, SME ACCESS
Loan, which taps funds from the capital market
Enterprise Development Centres
was launched in April 2005. The new scheme is

Serving Citizens Better Contributed by:
Ms Soo Cheng Ghee
e-Government Services
Senior Economist
Economics and Strategy Division
Today, more than 98 per cent of all public Ministry of Trade and Industry
services that can be delivered electronically are
Ministry of Transport
available online. Convenient access to the Internet
is a pre-requisite for the public to transact online
Infocomm Development Authority of Singapore
with the Government. Those without access to a
computer or the Internet can go to public libraries
and e-clubs at community centres to get online.
Government agencies have also set up self-service
terminals for the public to transact online. More
than 1,200 self-service Internet terminals have
been installed across 150 public service locations
since March 2005. This is part of the strategy to
gradually ‘migrate’ users from service counters
to online channels.
Addressing Community Needs
In February 2005, Connecting the Community,
an initiative which aimed to address a range of
needs of the family and the general community
started its first public trial. It involved 2,500 users
who tested solutions developed by four consortia
consisting of 23 organisations ranging from IT
solutions providers to Citizen’s Consultative
Committees (CCCs) and healthcare equipment
providers. Some of the solutions include alerts
activated using wireless technology for the aged
and real-time information alerts via electronic
notice boards at void decks.

3 With effect in May 2005, SGX-ST changed the methodology of computing its market capitalization by excluding inactive secondary foreign listings. This is to provide a more
accurate reflection of its market capitalization. Had SGX-ST used the same methodology it had applied in 2004, the market capitalization of the SGX Mainboard and the SESDAQ
would have been $526 billion, an increase of 23 per cent, from 2004’s $452 billion. This is due to a general increase in equity prices and the number of companies listed on
SGX-ST.
